Nick P</name>
<date>1597080057309</date>< rating>
3<//rating>
<text>I lived at Woodland park for three years and moved out about three years ago. I finally decided to write a review to help others looking for a place to live.

The property includes a lot of different building types from single family homes, small apartments buildings, and large buildings, so my experience may not be applicable to everyone.

For reference, I lived at the 665 Scofield Ave building.

At least at the time of my residence (and from looking at newer reviews), most of the buildings are old and in a relatively bad shape. However, the rent is about the most affordable I was able to find when moving to the Bay Area from college. At 1600 USD per month for a relatively large studio it was the best deal on paper (for bay area). So the question is whether quality of the community/buildings is an ok compromise for you for lower rent.

My apartment came with a free parking spot, but it would constantly get taken by guests or strangers since parking at the building I lived at was not gated. As a result I would have to occasionally negotiate with the office staff or security about parking at the main complex parking in the "Office" parking spot. This would be particularly challenging if coming back late. Also, I don't believe any of the offenders were ever towed. That car later died, so I didn't have this issue anymore.

Similar to other reviewers' experiences, kids would play in the inner yard all day, which would be very loud (no WFH in that place). The entrance gates would always be jammed up by other residents who would come out for a smoke without keys resulting in open entrance to anyone. The apartments also have giant windows facing the yard, which I always considered a burglary hazard (especially with the window right next to the door and locks), so during my stay there was one case of someone breaking into another apartment in that little complex.

Inner yard lights would some times break (not sure if maintenance-related or vandalism), so the yard would be pitch-black at night. The laundry facility was also dirty and the machines would be broken some of the time.

In my last year, there was also a roach problem, so I had to get some traps to get it under control.

At the end, I did end up getting my deposit back without much trouble and didn't have much trouble with the management team. Most people I interacted with were friendly and relatively helpful.

In conclusion, the reason why I'm giving this place 3 stars is because it's an ok place top live if you consider the low rent, location, and are willing to compromise with all of the community's problems and don't have high expectations of a rent controlled complex built in 60s/70s. For me it was a great kick-start to my apartment renting experience and while I personally would never rent here again unless the entire complex is renewed (not renovated, but more like rebuilt), this place has the lowest rent for the location so close to Palo Alto.</text>< pictures>
None</pictures>

<userid>104910820388319703671</userid><Name>Emily Noothernameneeded</Name><Time>1607069956017<//Time>< Rating>

< Review>
Visited this place on a chilly December evening. The gas burner by the outside tables along with the cute decor was more than enticing.  The place is run by a friendly and interesting English couple Anna and Tim who now call Solvang home.  There was a vast selection of wines and if you're unsure what to choose, Anna and Tim are excellent at guiding you through the options to suit your palate.  Due to Covid restrictions to have food with your wine order so I had a mixed plate tapas style of fruit, olives, hummus, sundried tomatoes  arugula lettuce, cheese and artisan bread.. it was a perfect meal to accompany the amazing wine.  I also discovered they serve cider, so I had to try one, for any cider drinkers I strongly recommend it. They also have beer on tap for those who are non-wine drinkers. This place is suitable for a date night or a wine sampling session, and in more normal times - a small social gathering.  There is every attention to detail and it's a lovely place to spend some time.  I'll definitely be back here.  Recommend!!!<//Review>

< review>
Fantastic wine, always!

Just wish they'd just dim the lighting in different ways to give an ambiance. It's always too bright to feel relaxed and therefore, emotionally connected with anyone (including your friends) there. As a potentially weekly customer couple, it stops us going and we think it's such a waste because otherwise we'd be there all the time.

<username>Greg Coolidge</username>< time>
1429765632714</time>
<rating>5</rating>< Review>
My wife and I have drank and tasted wine at the Wandering Dog numerous times over the last five years when visiting Santa Ynez.  In fact, we make it a point to always stop by this place at least one time on every weekend trip we have made during this period of time.  Without fail, the owner, C.T, has been friendly and attentive, answering all of our questions about the wine we were drinking, and also never failing to offer a great suggestion when asked "what would your drink among the wines you are pouring." As a result, my wife and I have often left the place in a state of happy and at times stumbling bliss while walking to our hotel across the street. This is one of m favorite wine bars/shops in California that I have visited.  I also do not understand one of the negative reviews I read that there are no local wines there.  The shop is packed with excellent Central Coast wines, including several from the Santa Ynez Valley and surrounding areas.  The shop also offers numerous excellent wines from around the world.<//Review>

We called the restaurant beforehand to see how long the wait was to get a table, and they said it was about 20-25 minutes. When we asked if we could make a reservation, they rudely told us that they don‚Äôt and hung up. We finally get there and are told that they had around the same wait time so we sat down. My girlfriend and I went here on the opening night. I've been to other Famous Dave's locations in Washington state, but this was the first time she had dined there.

We each ordered the 2 meat and 2 sides entree, and shared everything.  The highlights were the rib tips, cod, mac and cheese, beans, and garlic mashed potatoes.

</record></dataset><record>
< Text>
Had my dog with me and some time to kill while waiting to give a ride to a friend, so thought I'd do some some exploring. Saw the sign and entered a rather unassuming parking lot with no expectations. Both dog and I ended up really enjoying ourselves. Just past the small rectangular lot with parking and concrete picnic tables on one side, a sandy trail snaked through some low brush and through a cut in the small hill to reveal several rows of  20-40' sand  dunes dotted with clusters of brush as far as the eye could see in one direction, and perhaps 3-4 large dunes and valleys between the trailhead and the beach (which I never made it too). Instead I climbed the sliding face of one of the closest tallest dunes (not easy) and rested under a wind-swept tree along it's winding peak. It was a very bizarre sight, one side of this mount was pristine white sand and scrub, but the backside descended into a loamy, shady, forested area, that descended another 40' below the dune's base down to a set of trails that cris-crossed a dry stream bed. Time was up for exploring, but I'll definitely be back, next time allotting more exploration time. Lastly, you might think an area like that with it's many private hidden spots might be populated with transients and littered with trash, but none of either was to be seen. A potential nice place to get away with someone for an afternoon and find a fun spot to relax.<//Text>
